\DoxyCodeLine{43   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{44   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Section>                                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{45   \textcolor{comment}{/*    header\_inclusion                                                   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{46   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{47   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Title>                                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{48   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FreeType's header inclusion scheme                                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{49   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{50   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Abstract>                                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{51   \textcolor{comment}{/*    How client applications should include FreeType header files.      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{52   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{53   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{54   \textcolor{comment}{/*    To be as flexible as possible (and for historical reasons),        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{55   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FreeType uses a very special inclusion scheme to load header       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{56   \textcolor{comment}{/*    files, for example                                                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{57   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{58   \textcolor{comment}{/*    \{                                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{59   \textcolor{comment}{/*      \#include <ft2build.h>                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{60   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{61   \textcolor{comment}{/*      \#include FT\_FREETYPE\_H                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{62   \textcolor{comment}{/*      \#include FT\_OUTLINE\_H                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{63   \textcolor{comment}{/*    \}                                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{64   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{65   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A compiler and its preprocessor only needs an include path to find */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{66   \textcolor{comment}{/*    the file `ft2build.h'; the exact locations and names of the other  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{67   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FreeType header files are hidden by preprocessor macro names,      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{68   \textcolor{comment}{/*    loaded by `ft2build.h'.  The API documentation always gives the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{69   \textcolor{comment}{/*    header macro name needed for a particular function.                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{70   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{71 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{72 }
\DoxyCodeLine{73 }
\DoxyCodeLine{74 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{75   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{76   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Section>                                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{77   \textcolor{comment}{/*    user\_allocation                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{78   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{79   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Title>                                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{80   \textcolor{comment}{/*    User allocation                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{81   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{82   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Abstract>                                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{83   \textcolor{comment}{/*    How client applications should allocate FreeType data structures.  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{84   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{85   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{86   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FreeType assumes that structures allocated by the user and passed  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{87   \textcolor{comment}{/*    as arguments are zeroed out except for the actual data.  In other  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{88   \textcolor{comment}{/*    words, it is recommended to use `calloc' (or variants of it)       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{89   \textcolor{comment}{/*    instead of `malloc' for allocation.                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{90   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{91 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}

\DoxyCodeLine{261 }
\DoxyCodeLine{262 }
\DoxyCodeLine{263 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{264   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{265   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Struct>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{266   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_Glyph\_Metrics                                                   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{267   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{268   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{269   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A structure used to model the metrics of a single glyph.  The      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{270   \textcolor{comment}{/*    values are expressed in 26.6 fractional pixel format; if the flag  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{271   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_LOAD\_NO\_SCALE has been used while loading the glyph, values    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{272   \textcolor{comment}{/*    are expressed in font units instead.                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{273   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{274   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Fields>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{275   \textcolor{comment}{/*    width ::                                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{276   \textcolor{comment}{/*      The glyph's width.                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{277   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{278   \textcolor{comment}{/*    height ::                                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{279   \textcolor{comment}{/*      The glyph's height.                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{280   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{281   \textcolor{comment}{/*    horiBearingX ::                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{282   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Left side bearing for horizontal layout.                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{283   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{284   \textcolor{comment}{/*    horiBearingY ::                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{285   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Top side bearing for horizontal layout.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{286   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{287   \textcolor{comment}{/*    horiAdvance ::                                                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{288   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Advance width for horizontal layout.                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{289   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{290   \textcolor{comment}{/*    vertBearingX ::                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{291   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Left side bearing for vertical layout.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{292   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{293   \textcolor{comment}{/*    vertBearingY ::                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{294   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Top side bearing for vertical layout.  Larger positive values    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{295   \textcolor{comment}{/*      mean further below the vertical glyph origin.                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{296   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{297   \textcolor{comment}{/*    vertAdvance ::                                                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{298   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Advance height for vertical layout.  Positive values mean the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{299   \textcolor{comment}{/*      glyph has a positive advance downward.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{300   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{301   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{302   \textcolor{comment}{/*    If not disabled with @FT\_LOAD\_NO\_HINTING, the values represent     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{303   \textcolor{comment}{/*    dimensions of the hinted glyph (in case hinting is applicable).    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{304   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{305   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Stroking a glyph with an outside border does not increase          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{306   \textcolor{comment}{/*    `horiAdvance' or `vertAdvance'; you have to manually adjust these  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{307   \textcolor{comment}{/*    values to account for the added width and height.                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{308   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{309   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{struct  }\mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__Glyph__Metrics__}{FT\_Glyph\_Metrics\_}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{310   \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{311     FT\_Pos  width;}
\DoxyCodeLine{312     FT\_Pos  height;}
\DoxyCodeLine{313 }
\DoxyCodeLine{314     FT\_Pos  horiBearingX;}
\DoxyCodeLine{315     FT\_Pos  horiBearingY;}
\DoxyCodeLine{316     FT\_Pos  horiAdvance;}
\DoxyCodeLine{317 }
\DoxyCodeLine{318     FT\_Pos  vertBearingX;}
\DoxyCodeLine{319     FT\_Pos  vertBearingY;}
\DoxyCodeLine{320     FT\_Pos  vertAdvance;}
\DoxyCodeLine{321 }
\DoxyCodeLine{322   \} FT\_Glyph\_Metrics;}
\DoxyCodeLine{323 }
\DoxyCodeLine{324 }
\DoxyCodeLine{325 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{326   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{327   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Struct>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{328   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_Bitmap\_Size                                                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{329   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{330   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{331   \textcolor{comment}{/*    This structure models the metrics of a bitmap strike (i.e., a set  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{332   \textcolor{comment}{/*    of glyphs for a given point size and resolution) in a bitmap font. */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{333   \textcolor{comment}{/*    It is used for the `available\_sizes' field of @FT\_Face.            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{334   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{335   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Fields>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{336   \textcolor{comment}{/*    height :: The vertical distance, in pixels, between two            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{337   \textcolor{comment}{/*              consecutive baselines.  It is always positive.           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{338   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{339   \textcolor{comment}{/*    width  :: The average width, in pixels, of all glyphs in the       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{340   \textcolor{comment}{/*              strike.                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{341   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{342   \textcolor{comment}{/*    size   :: The nominal size of the strike in 26.6 fractional        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{343   \textcolor{comment}{/*              points.  This field is not very useful.                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{344   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{345   \textcolor{comment}{/*    x\_ppem :: The horizontal ppem (nominal width) in 26.6 fractional   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{346   \textcolor{comment}{/*              pixels.                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{347   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{348   \textcolor{comment}{/*    y\_ppem :: The vertical ppem (nominal height) in 26.6 fractional    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{349   \textcolor{comment}{/*              pixels.                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{350   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{351   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{352   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Windows FNT:                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{353   \textcolor{comment}{/*      The nominal size given in a FNT font is not reliable.  Thus when */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{354   \textcolor{comment}{/*      the driver finds it incorrect, it sets `size' to some calculated */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{355   \textcolor{comment}{/*      values and sets `x\_ppem' and `y\_ppem' to the pixel width and     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{356   \textcolor{comment}{/*      height given in the font, respectively.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{357   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{358   \textcolor{comment}{/*    TrueType embedded bitmaps:                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{359   \textcolor{comment}{/*      `size', `width', and `height' values are not contained in the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{360   \textcolor{comment}{/*      bitmap strike itself.  They are computed from the global font    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{361   \textcolor{comment}{/*      parameters.                                                      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{362   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{363   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{struct  }\mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__Bitmap__Size__}{FT\_Bitmap\_Size\_}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{364   \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{365     FT\_Short  height;}
\DoxyCodeLine{366     FT\_Short  width;}
\DoxyCodeLine{367 }
\DoxyCodeLine{368     FT\_Pos    size;}
\DoxyCodeLine{369 }
\DoxyCodeLine{370     FT\_Pos    x\_ppem;}
\DoxyCodeLine{371     FT\_Pos    y\_ppem;}
\DoxyCodeLine{372 }
\DoxyCodeLine{373   \} \mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__Bitmap__Size__}{FT\_Bitmap\_Size}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{374 }

\DoxyCodeLine{386   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Type>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{387   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_Library                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{388   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{389   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{390   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A handle to a FreeType library instance.  Each `library' is        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{391   \textcolor{comment}{/*    completely independent from the others; it is the `root' of a set  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{392   \textcolor{comment}{/*    of objects like fonts, faces, sizes, etc.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{393   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{394   \textcolor{comment}{/*    It also embeds a memory manager (see @FT\_Memory), as well as a     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{395   \textcolor{comment}{/*    scan-\/line converter object (see @FT\_Raster).                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{396   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{397   \textcolor{comment}{/*    In multi-\/threaded applications, make sure that the same FT\_Library */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{398   \textcolor{comment}{/*    object or any of its children doesn't get accessed in parallel.    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{399   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{400   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{401   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Library objects are normally created by @FT\_Init\_FreeType, and     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{402   \textcolor{comment}{/*    destroyed with @FT\_Done\_FreeType.  If you need reference-\/counting  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{403   \textcolor{comment}{/*    (cf. @FT\_Reference\_Library), use @FT\_New\_Library and               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{404   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_Done\_Library.                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{405   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{406   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{struct }FT\_LibraryRec\_  *FT\_Library;}

\DoxyCodeLine{499   \textcolor{comment}{/*    transformation that in turn is used to load and hint glyphs and    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{500   \textcolor{comment}{/*    metrics.                                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{501   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{502   \textcolor{comment}{/*    You can use @FT\_Set\_Char\_Size, @FT\_Set\_Pixel\_Sizes,                */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{504   \textcolor{comment}{/*    (i.e., the scaling values) of the active @FT\_Size.                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{505   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{506   \textcolor{comment}{/*    You can use @FT\_New\_Size to create additional size objects for a   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{507   \textcolor{comment}{/*    given @FT\_Face, but they won't be used by other functions until    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{508   \textcolor{comment}{/*    you activate it through @FT\_Activate\_Size.  Only one size can be   */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{511   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Also>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{512   \textcolor{comment}{/*    See @FT\_SizeRec for the publicly accessible fields of a given size */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{514   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{519   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{520   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Type>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{521   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_GlyphSlot                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{522   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{523   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{524   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A handle to a given `glyph slot'.  A slot is a container where it  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{525   \textcolor{comment}{/*    is possible to load any of the glyphs contained in its parent      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{526   \textcolor{comment}{/*    face.                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{527   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{528   \textcolor{comment}{/*    In other words, each time you call @FT\_Load\_Glyph or               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{529   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_Load\_Char, the slot's content is erased by the new glyph data, */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{530   \textcolor{comment}{/*    i.e., the glyph's metrics, its image (bitmap or outline), and      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{531   \textcolor{comment}{/*    other control information.                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{532   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{533   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Also>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{534   \textcolor{comment}{/*    See @FT\_GlyphSlotRec for the publicly accessible glyph fields.     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{535   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{538 }
\DoxyCodeLine{539 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{540   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{541   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Type>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{542   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_CharMap                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{543   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{544   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{545   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A handle to a given character map.  A charmap is used to translate */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{546   \textcolor{comment}{/*    character codes in a given encoding into glyph indexes for its     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{547   \textcolor{comment}{/*    parent's face.  Some font formats may provide several charmaps per */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{548   \textcolor{comment}{/*    font.                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{549   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{550   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Each face object owns zero or more charmaps, but only one of them  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{551   \textcolor{comment}{/*    can be `active' and used by @FT\_Get\_Char\_Index or @FT\_Load\_Char.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{552   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{553   \textcolor{comment}{/*    The list of available charmaps in a face is available through the  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{554   \textcolor{comment}{/*    `face-\/>num\_charmaps' and `face-\/>charmaps' fields of @FT\_FaceRec.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{555   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{556   \textcolor{comment}{/*    The currently active charmap is available as `face-\/>charmap'.      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{557   \textcolor{comment}{/*    You should call @FT\_Set\_Charmap to change it.                      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{558   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{559   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{560   \textcolor{comment}{/*    When a new face is created (either through @FT\_New\_Face or         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{561   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_Open\_Face), the library looks for a Unicode charmap within     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{562   \textcolor{comment}{/*    the list and automatically activates it.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{563   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{564   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Also>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{565   \textcolor{comment}{/*    See @FT\_CharMapRec for the publicly accessible fields of a given   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{566   \textcolor{comment}{/*    character map.                                                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{567   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{568   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{struct }\mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__CharMapRec__}{FT\_CharMapRec\_}}*  \mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__CharMapRec__}{FT\_CharMap}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{569 }
\DoxyCodeLine{570 }
\DoxyCodeLine{571 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{572   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{573   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Macro>                                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{574   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENC\_TAG                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{575   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{576   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{577   \textcolor{comment}{/*    This macro converts four-\/letter tags into an unsigned long.  It is */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{578   \textcolor{comment}{/*    used to define `encoding' identifiers (see @FT\_Encoding).          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{579   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{580   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{581   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Since many 16-\/bit compilers don't like 32-\/bit enumerations, you    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{582   \textcolor{comment}{/*    should redefine this macro in case of problems to something like   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{583   \textcolor{comment}{/*    this:                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{584   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{585   \textcolor{comment}{/*    \{                                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{586   \textcolor{comment}{/*      \#define FT\_ENC\_TAG( value, a, b, c, d )  value                   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{587   \textcolor{comment}{/*    \}                                                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{588   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{589   \textcolor{comment}{/*    to get a simple enumeration without assigning special numbers.     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{590   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{591 }
\DoxyCodeLine{592 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#ifndef FT\_ENC\_TAG}}
\DoxyCodeLine{593 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#define FT\_ENC\_TAG( value, a, b, c, d )         \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{594 \textcolor{preprocessor}{          value = ( ( (FT\_UInt32)(a) << 24 ) |  \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{595 \textcolor{preprocessor}{                    ( (FT\_UInt32)(b) << 16 ) |  \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{596 \textcolor{preprocessor}{                    ( (FT\_UInt32)(c) <<  8 ) |  \(\backslash\)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{597 \textcolor{preprocessor}{                      (FT\_UInt32)(d)         )}}
\DoxyCodeLine{598 }
\DoxyCodeLine{599 \textcolor{preprocessor}{\#endif }\textcolor{comment}{/* FT\_ENC\_TAG */}\textcolor{preprocessor}{}}
\DoxyCodeLine{600 }
\DoxyCodeLine{601 }
\DoxyCodeLine{602 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{603   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{604   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Enum>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{605   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_Encoding                                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{606   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{607   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{608   \textcolor{comment}{/*    An enumeration used to specify character sets supported by         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{609   \textcolor{comment}{/*    charmaps.  Used in the @FT\_Select\_Charmap API function.            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{610   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{611   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{612   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Despite the name, this enumeration lists specific character        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{613   \textcolor{comment}{/*    repertories (i.e., charsets), and not text encoding methods (e.g., */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{614   \textcolor{comment}{/*    UTF-\/8, UTF-\/16, etc.).                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{615   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{616   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Other encodings might be defined in the future.                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{617   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{618   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Values>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{619   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_NONE ::                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{620   \textcolor{comment}{/*      The encoding value\string~0 is reserved.                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{621   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{622   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_UNICODE ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{623   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the Unicode character set.  This value covers     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{624   \textcolor{comment}{/*      all versions of the Unicode repertoire, including ASCII and      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{625   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Latin-\/1.  Most fonts include a Unicode charmap, but not all      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{626   \textcolor{comment}{/*      of them.                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{627   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{628   \textcolor{comment}{/*      For example, if you want to access Unicode value U+1F028 (and    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{629   \textcolor{comment}{/*      the font contains it), use value 0x1F028 as the input value for  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{630   \textcolor{comment}{/*      @FT\_Get\_Char\_Index.                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{631   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{632   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_SYMBOL ::                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{633   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the Microsoft Symbol encoding, used to encode     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{634   \textcolor{comment}{/*      mathematical symbols in the 32..255 character code range.  For   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{635   \textcolor{comment}{/*      more information, see                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{636   \textcolor{comment}{/*      `http://www.kostis.net/charsets/symbol.htm'.                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{637   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{638   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_SJIS ::                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{639   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to Japanese SJIS encoding.  More info at             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{640   \textcolor{comment}{/*      at `http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shift\_JIS'.                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{641   \textcolor{comment}{/*      See note on multi-\/byte encodings below.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{642   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{643   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_GB2312 ::                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{644   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to an encoding system for Simplified Chinese as used */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{645   \textcolor{comment}{/*      used in mainland China.                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{646   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{647   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_BIG5 ::                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{648   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to an encoding system for Traditional Chinese as     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{649   \textcolor{comment}{/*      used in Taiwan and Hong Kong.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{650   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{651   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_WANSUNG ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{652   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the Korean encoding system known as Wansung.      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{653   \textcolor{comment}{/*      For more information see                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{654   \textcolor{comment}{/*      `http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-\/US/goglobal/cc305154'.             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{655   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{656   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_JOHAB ::                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{657   \textcolor{comment}{/*      The Korean standard character set (KS\string~C 5601-\/1992), which        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{658   \textcolor{comment}{/*      corresponds to MS Windows code page 1361.  This character set    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{659   \textcolor{comment}{/*      includes all possible Hangeul character combinations.            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{660   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{661   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_LATIN\_1 ::                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{662   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to a Latin-\/1 encoding as defined in a Type\string~1         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{663   \textcolor{comment}{/*      PostScript font.  It is limited to 256 character codes.          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{664   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{665   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_STANDARD ::                                      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{666   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the Adobe Standard encoding, as found in Type\string~1,  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{667   \textcolor{comment}{/*      CFF, and OpenType/CFF fonts.  It is limited to 256 character     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{668   \textcolor{comment}{/*      codes.                                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{669   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{670   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_EXPERT ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{671   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the Adobe Expert encoding, as found in Type\string~1,    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{672   \textcolor{comment}{/*      CFF, and OpenType/CFF fonts.  It is limited to 256 character     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{673   \textcolor{comment}{/*      codes.                                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{674   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{675   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_CUSTOM ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{676   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to a custom encoding, as found in Type\string~1, CFF, and   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{677   \textcolor{comment}{/*      OpenType/CFF fonts.  It is limited to 256 character codes.       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{678   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{679   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_APPLE\_ROMAN ::                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{680   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Corresponds to the 8-\/bit Apple roman encoding.  Many TrueType    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{681   \textcolor{comment}{/*      and OpenType fonts contain a charmap for this encoding, since    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{682   \textcolor{comment}{/*      older versions of Mac OS are able to use it.                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{683   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{684   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_OLD\_LATIN\_2 ::                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{685   \textcolor{comment}{/*      This value is deprecated and was never used nor reported by      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{686   \textcolor{comment}{/*      FreeType.  Don't use or test for it.                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{687   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{688   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_SJIS ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{689   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Same as FT\_ENCODING\_SJIS.  Deprecated.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{690   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{691   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_GB2312 ::                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{692   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Same as FT\_ENCODING\_GB2312.  Deprecated.                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{693   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{694   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_BIG5 ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{695   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Same as FT\_ENCODING\_BIG5.  Deprecated.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{696   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{697   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_WANSUNG ::                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{698   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Same as FT\_ENCODING\_WANSUNG.  Deprecated.                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{699   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{700   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_JOHAB ::                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{701   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Same as FT\_ENCODING\_JOHAB.  Deprecated.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{702   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{703   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{704   \textcolor{comment}{/*    By default, FreeType automatically synthesizes a Unicode charmap   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{705   \textcolor{comment}{/*    for PostScript fonts, using their glyph names dictionaries.        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{706   \textcolor{comment}{/*    However, it also reports the encodings defined explicitly in the   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{707   \textcolor{comment}{/*    font file, for the cases when they are needed, with the Adobe      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{708   \textcolor{comment}{/*    values as well.                                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{709   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{710   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_NONE is set by the BDF and PCF drivers if the charmap  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{711   \textcolor{comment}{/*    is neither Unicode nor ISO-\/8859-\/1 (otherwise it is set to          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{712   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_UNICODE).  Use @FT\_Get\_BDF\_Charset\_ID to find out      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{713   \textcolor{comment}{/*    which encoding is really present.  If, for example, the            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{714   \textcolor{comment}{/*    `cs\_registry' field is `KOI8' and the `cs\_encoding' field is `R',  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{715   \textcolor{comment}{/*    the font is encoded in KOI8-\/R.                                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{716   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{717   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_NONE is always set (with a single exception) by the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{718   \textcolor{comment}{/*    winfonts driver.  Use @FT\_Get\_WinFNT\_Header and examine the        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{719   \textcolor{comment}{/*    `charset' field of the @FT\_WinFNT\_HeaderRec structure to find out  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{720   \textcolor{comment}{/*    which encoding is really present.  For example,                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{721   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_WinFNT\_ID\_CP1251 (204) means Windows code page 1251 (for       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{722   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Russian).                                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{723   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{724   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_NONE is set if `platform\_id' is @TT\_PLATFORM\_MACINTOSH */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{725   \textcolor{comment}{/*    and `encoding\_id' is not @TT\_MAC\_ID\_ROMAN (otherwise it is set to  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{726   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_ENCODING\_APPLE\_ROMAN).                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{727   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{728   \textcolor{comment}{/*    If `platform\_id' is @TT\_PLATFORM\_MACINTOSH, use the function       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{729   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_Get\_CMap\_Language\_ID to query the Mac language ID that may     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{730   \textcolor{comment}{/*    be needed to be able to distinguish Apple encoding variants.  See  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{731   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{732   \textcolor{comment}{/*      http://www.unicode.org/Public/MAPPINGS/VENDORS/APPLE/Readme.txt  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{733   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{734   \textcolor{comment}{/*    to get an idea how to do that.  Basically, if the language ID      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{735   \textcolor{comment}{/*    is\string~0, don't use it, otherwise subtract 1 from the language ID.     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{736   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Then examine `encoding\_id'.  If, for example, `encoding\_id' is     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{737   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @TT\_MAC\_ID\_ROMAN and the language ID (minus\string~1) is                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{738   \textcolor{comment}{/*    `TT\_MAC\_LANGID\_GREEK', it is the Greek encoding, not Roman.        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{739   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @TT\_MAC\_ID\_ARABIC with `TT\_MAC\_LANGID\_FARSI' means the Farsi       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{740   \textcolor{comment}{/*    variant the Arabic encoding.                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{741   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{742   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{enum}  FT\_Encoding\_}
\DoxyCodeLine{743   \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{744     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_NONE, 0, 0, 0, 0 ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{745 }

\DoxyCodeLine{747     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_UNICODE,   \textcolor{charliteral}{'u'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'n'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'i'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'c'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{748 }
\DoxyCodeLine{749     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_SJIS,    \textcolor{charliteral}{'s'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'j'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'i'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'s'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{750     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_GB2312,  \textcolor{charliteral}{'g'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'b'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{' '}, \textcolor{charliteral}{' '} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{751     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_BIG5,    \textcolor{charliteral}{'b'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'i'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'g'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'5'} ),}

\DoxyCodeLine{759     FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_WANSUNG = FT\_ENCODING\_WANSUNG,}
\DoxyCodeLine{760     FT\_ENCODING\_MS\_JOHAB   = FT\_ENCODING\_JOHAB,}
\DoxyCodeLine{761 }
\DoxyCodeLine{762     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_STANDARD, \textcolor{charliteral}{'A'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'D'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'O'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'B'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{763     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_EXPERT,   \textcolor{charliteral}{'A'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'D'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'B'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'E'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{764     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_CUSTOM,   \textcolor{charliteral}{'A'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'D'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'B'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'C'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{765     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_ADOBE\_LATIN\_1,  \textcolor{charliteral}{'l'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'a'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'t'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'1'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{766 }
\DoxyCodeLine{767     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_OLD\_LATIN\_2, \textcolor{charliteral}{'l'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'a'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'t'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'2'} ),}
\DoxyCodeLine{768 }
\DoxyCodeLine{769     FT\_ENC\_TAG( FT\_ENCODING\_APPLE\_ROMAN, \textcolor{charliteral}{'a'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'r'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'m'}, \textcolor{charliteral}{'n'} )}
\DoxyCodeLine{770 }
\DoxyCodeLine{771   \} FT\_Encoding;}
\DoxyCodeLine{772 }

\DoxyCodeLine{813   \textcolor{comment}{/*                   comes from the TrueType specification and should be */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{814   \textcolor{comment}{/*                   emulated similarly.                                 */}}

\DoxyCodeLine{850 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{851   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{852   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Struct>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{853   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FaceRec                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{854   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{855   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{856   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FreeType root face class structure.  A face object models a        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{857   \textcolor{comment}{/*    typeface in a font file.                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{858   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{859   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Fields>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{860   \textcolor{comment}{/*    num\_faces           :: The number of faces in the font file.  Some */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{861   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           font formats can have multiple faces in     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{862   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           a font file.                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{863   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{864   \textcolor{comment}{/*    face\_index          :: The index of the face in the font file.  It */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{865   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           is set to\string~0 if there is only one face in    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{866   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           the font file.                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{867   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{868   \textcolor{comment}{/*    face\_flags          :: A set of bit flags that give important      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{869   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           information about the face; see             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{870   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           @FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_XXX for the details.          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{871   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{872   \textcolor{comment}{/*    style\_flags         :: A set of bit flags indicating the style of  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{873   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           the face; see @FT\_STYLE\_FLAG\_XXX for the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{874   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           details.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{875   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{876   \textcolor{comment}{/*    num\_glyphs          :: The number of glyphs in the face.  If the   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{877   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           face is scalable and has sbits (see         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{878   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `num\_fixed\_sizes'), it is set to the number */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{879   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           of outline glyphs.                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{880   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{881   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           For CID-\/keyed fonts, this value gives the   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{882   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           highest CID used in the font.               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{883   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{884   \textcolor{comment}{/*    family\_name         :: The face's family name.  This is an ASCII   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{885   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           string, usually in English, that describes  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{886   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           the typeface's family (like `Times New      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{887   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           Roman', `Bodoni', `Garamond', etc).  This   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{888   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           is a least common denominator used to list  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{889   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           fonts.  Some formats (TrueType \& OpenType)  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{890   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           provide localized and Unicode versions of   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{891   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           this string.  Applications should use the   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{892   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           format specific interface to access them.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{893   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           Can be NULL (e.g., in fonts embedded in a   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{894   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           PDF file).                                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{895   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{896   \textcolor{comment}{/*    style\_name          :: The face's style name.  This is an ASCII    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{897   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           string, usually in English, that describes  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{898   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           the typeface's style (like `Italic',        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{899   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `Bold', `Condensed', etc).  Not all font    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{900   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           formats provide a style name, so this field */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{901   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           is optional, and can be set to NULL.  As    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{902   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           for `family\_name', some formats provide     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{903   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           localized and Unicode versions of this      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{904   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           string.  Applications should use the format */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{905   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           specific interface to access them.          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{906   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{907   \textcolor{comment}{/*    num\_fixed\_sizes     :: The number of bitmap strikes in the face.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{908   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           Even if the face is scalable, there might   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{909   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           still be bitmap strikes, which are called   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{910   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `sbits' in that case.                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{911   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{912   \textcolor{comment}{/*    available\_sizes     :: An array of @FT\_Bitmap\_Size for all bitmap  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{913   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           strikes in the face.  It is set to NULL if  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{914   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           there is no bitmap strike.                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{915   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{916   \textcolor{comment}{/*    num\_charmaps        :: The number of charmaps in the face.         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{917   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{918   \textcolor{comment}{/*    charmaps            :: An array of the charmaps of the face.       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{919   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{920   \textcolor{comment}{/*    generic             :: A field reserved for client uses.  See the  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{921   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           @FT\_Generic type description.               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{922   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{923   \textcolor{comment}{/*    bbox                :: The font bounding box.  Coordinates are     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{924   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           expressed in font units (see                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{925   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `units\_per\_EM').  The box is large enough   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{926   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           to contain any glyph from the font.  Thus,  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{927   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `bbox.yMax' can be seen as the `maximum     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{928   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           ascender', and `bbox.yMin' as the `minimum  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{929   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           descender'.  Only relevant for scalable     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{930   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           formats.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{931   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{932   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           Note that the bounding box might be off by  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{933   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           (at least) one pixel for hinted fonts.  See */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{934   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           @FT\_Size\_Metrics for further discussion.    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{935   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{936   \textcolor{comment}{/*    units\_per\_EM        :: The number of font units per EM square for  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{937   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           this face.  This is typically 2048 for      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{938   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           TrueType fonts, and 1000 for Type\string~1 fonts.  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{939   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           Only relevant for scalable formats.         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{940   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{941   \textcolor{comment}{/*    ascender            :: The typographic ascender of the face,       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{942   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           expressed in font units.  For font formats  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{943   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           not having this information, it is set to   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{944   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `bbox.yMax'.  Only relevant for scalable    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{945   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           formats.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{946   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{947   \textcolor{comment}{/*    descender           :: The typographic descender of the face,      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{948   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           expressed in font units.  For font formats  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{949   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           not having this information, it is set to   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{950   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `bbox.yMin'.  Note that this field is       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{951   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           usually negative.  Only relevant for        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{952   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           scalable formats.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{953   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{954   \textcolor{comment}{/*    height              :: This value is the vertical distance         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{955   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           between two consecutive baselines,          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{956   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           expressed in font units.  It is always      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{957   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           positive.  Only relevant for scalable       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{958   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           formats.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{959   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{960   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           If you want the global glyph height, use    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{961   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           `ascender -\/ descender'.                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{962   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{963   \textcolor{comment}{/*    max\_advance\_width   :: The maximum advance width, in font units,   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{964   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           for all glyphs in this face.  This can be   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{965   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           used to make word wrapping computations     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{966   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           faster.  Only relevant for scalable         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{967   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           formats.                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{968   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{969   \textcolor{comment}{/*    max\_advance\_height  :: The maximum advance height, in font units,  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{970   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           for all glyphs in this face.  This is only  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{971   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           relevant for vertical layouts, and is set   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{972   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           to `height' for fonts that do not provide   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{973   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           vertical metrics.  Only relevant for        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{974   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           scalable formats.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{975   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{976   \textcolor{comment}{/*    underline\_position  :: The position, in font units, of the         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{977   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           underline line for this face.  It is the    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{978   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           center of the underlining stem.  Only       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{979   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           relevant for scalable formats.              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{980   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{981   \textcolor{comment}{/*    underline\_thickness :: The thickness, in font units, of the        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{982   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           underline for this face.  Only relevant for */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{983   \textcolor{comment}{/*                           scalable formats.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{984   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{985   \textcolor{comment}{/*    glyph               :: The face's associated glyph slot(s).        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{986   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{987   \textcolor{comment}{/*    size                :: The current active size for this face.      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{988   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{989   \textcolor{comment}{/*    charmap             :: The current active charmap for this face.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{990   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{991   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Note>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{992   \textcolor{comment}{/*    Fields may be changed after a call to @FT\_Attach\_File or           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{993   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_Attach\_Stream.                                                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{994   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{995   \textcolor{keyword}{typedef} \textcolor{keyword}{struct  }\mbox{\hyperlink{structFT__FaceRec__}{FT\_FaceRec\_}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{996   \{}

\DoxyCodeLine{1052 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1053 }
\DoxyCodeLine{1054 \textcolor{comment}{  /*************************************************************************/}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1055   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1056   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Enum>                                                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1057   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_XXX                                                   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1058   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1059   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Description>                                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1060   \textcolor{comment}{/*    A list of bit flags used in the `face\_flags' field of the          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1061   \textcolor{comment}{/*    @FT\_FaceRec structure.  They inform client applications of         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1062   \textcolor{comment}{/*    properties of the corresponding face.                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1063   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1064   \textcolor{comment}{/* <Values>                                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1065   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_SCALABLE ::                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1066   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains outline glyphs.  This doesn't   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1067   \textcolor{comment}{/*      prevent bitmap strikes, i.e., a face can have both this and      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1068   \textcolor{comment}{/*      and @FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_FIXED\_SIZES set.                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1069   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1070   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_FIXED\_SIZES ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1071   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains bitmap strikes.  See also the   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1072   \textcolor{comment}{/*      `num\_fixed\_sizes' and `available\_sizes' fields of @FT\_FaceRec.   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1073   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1074   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_FIXED\_WIDTH ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1075   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains fixed-\/width characters (like    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1076   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Courier, Lucido, MonoType, etc.).                                */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1077   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1078   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_SFNT ::                                               */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1079   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face uses the `sfnt' storage scheme.  For     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1080   \textcolor{comment}{/*      now, this means TrueType and OpenType.                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1081   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1082   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_HORIZONTAL ::                                         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1083   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains horizontal glyph metrics.  This */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1084   \textcolor{comment}{/*      should be set for all common formats.                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1085   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1086   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_VERTICAL ::                                           */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1087   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains vertical glyph metrics.  This   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1088   \textcolor{comment}{/*      is only available in some formats, not all of them.              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1089   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1090   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_KERNING ::                                            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1091   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the face contains kerning information.  If set,   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1092   \textcolor{comment}{/*      the kerning distance can be retrieved through the function       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1093   \textcolor{comment}{/*      @FT\_Get\_Kerning.  Otherwise the function always return the       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1094   \textcolor{comment}{/*      vector (0,0).  Note that FreeType doesn't handle kerning data    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1095   \textcolor{comment}{/*      from the `GPOS' table (as present in some OpenType fonts).       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1096   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1097   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_FAST\_GLYPHS ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1098   \textcolor{comment}{/*      THIS FLAG IS DEPRECATED.  DO NOT USE OR TEST IT.                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1099   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1100   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_MULTIPLE\_MASTERS ::                                   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1101   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the font contains multiple masters and is capable */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1102   \textcolor{comment}{/*      of interpolating between them.  See the multiple-\/masters         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1103   \textcolor{comment}{/*      specific API for details.                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1104   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1105   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_GLYPH\_NAMES ::                                        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1106   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Indicates that the font contains glyph names that can be         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1107   \textcolor{comment}{/*      retrieved through @FT\_Get\_Glyph\_Name.  Note that some TrueType   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1108   \textcolor{comment}{/*      fonts contain broken glyph name tables.  Use the function        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1109   \textcolor{comment}{/*      @FT\_Has\_PS\_Glyph\_Names when needed.                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1110   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1111   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_EXTERNAL\_STREAM ::                                    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1112   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Used internally by FreeType to indicate that a face's stream was */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1113   \textcolor{comment}{/*      provided by the client application and should not be destroyed   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1114   \textcolor{comment}{/*      when @FT\_Done\_Face is called.  Don't read or test this flag.     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1115   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1116   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_HINTER ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1117   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Set if the font driver has a hinting machine of its own.  For    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1118   \textcolor{comment}{/*      example, with TrueType fonts, it makes sense to use data from    */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1119   \textcolor{comment}{/*      the SFNT `gasp' table only if the native TrueType hinting engine */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1120   \textcolor{comment}{/*      (with the bytecode interpreter) is available and active.         */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1121   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1122   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_CID\_KEYED ::                                          */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1123   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Set if the font is CID-\/keyed.  In that case, the font is not     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1124   \textcolor{comment}{/*      accessed by glyph indices but by CID values.  For subsetted      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1125   \textcolor{comment}{/*      CID-\/keyed fonts this has the consequence that not all index      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1126   \textcolor{comment}{/*      values are a valid argument to FT\_Load\_Glyph.  Only the CID      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1127   \textcolor{comment}{/*      values for which corresponding glyphs in the subsetted font      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1128   \textcolor{comment}{/*      exist make FT\_Load\_Glyph return successfully; in all other cases */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1129   \textcolor{comment}{/*      you get an `FT\_Err\_Invalid\_Argument' error.                      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1130   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1131   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Note that CID-\/keyed fonts that are in an SFNT wrapper don't      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1132   \textcolor{comment}{/*      have this flag set since the glyphs are accessed in the normal   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1133   \textcolor{comment}{/*      way (using contiguous indices); the `CID-\/ness' isn't visible to  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1134   \textcolor{comment}{/*      the application.                                                 */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1135   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1136   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_TRICKY ::                                             */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1137   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Set if the font is `tricky', this is, it always needs the        */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1138   \textcolor{comment}{/*      font format's native hinting engine to get a reasonable result.  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1139   \textcolor{comment}{/*      A typical example is the Chinese font `mingli.ttf' that uses     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1140   \textcolor{comment}{/*      TrueType bytecode instructions to move and scale all of its      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1141   \textcolor{comment}{/*      subglyphs.                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1142   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1143   \textcolor{comment}{/*      It is not possible to autohint such fonts using                  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1144   \textcolor{comment}{/*      @FT\_LOAD\_FORCE\_AUTOHINT; it will also ignore                     */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1145   \textcolor{comment}{/*      @FT\_LOAD\_NO\_HINTING.  You have to set both @FT\_LOAD\_NO\_HINTING   */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1146   \textcolor{comment}{/*      and @FT\_LOAD\_NO\_AUTOHINT to really disable hinting; however, you */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1147   \textcolor{comment}{/*      probably never want this except for demonstration purposes.      */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1148   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1149   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Currently, there are about a dozen TrueType fonts in the list of */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1150   \textcolor{comment}{/*      tricky fonts; they are hard-\/coded in file `ttobjs.c'.            */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1151   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1152   \textcolor{comment}{/*    FT\_FACE\_FLAG\_COLOR ::                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1153   \textcolor{comment}{/*      Set if the font has color glyph tables.  To access color glyphs  */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1154   \textcolor{comment}{/*      use @FT\_LOAD\_COLOR.                                              */}}
\DoxyCodeLine{1155   \textcolor{comment}{/*                                                                       */}}
